O, sons, because I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, by the fulfillment of it its end is achieved in it, and by the expositions of it, and by the declarations of it, it is my view that you complete it with this treatise, which is a part of the operation with me, so it is my surgery.
Because the operation with me is widespread in our region and in our time completely private, while many risk the science of it, and its knowledge is held hostage; and there remain of it only some small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have been altered and become subject to those errors and inaccuracies because their clauses are the understandings of it and the force of it and the art are elongated.
And it is seen to me that you vivify it with the ordering of this treatise in that according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and for that it may come with the forms of the tools of cautery and of the other instruments of the work as it may be by addition of the declaration, and by preparation of it, which cause is necessary.
But the cause for which no good artificer with his hand is found in this our time, is because the art of medicine is long, and that it requires the actor to be beforehand exercised in the science of anatomy, which reconciles Gualia because he knows the joints of the members and the forms of those, and the connection and separation of them; and he had the knowledge of the bones, the nerves and the cartilages, the number of those, and the growth of them; and of the pulsating veins and the quiet ones, and the places of the emission of them.
And for that reason, it is said by Ypocras that with a name is little, but in the work is much, and most of all in the art of the hand.
But we have already said that in the introduction of this book; because whoever does not know what we have said of anatomy, it is not evacuated that he does not fall into error for which many men die, as I have seen too many of those, because some are formed in this science and cast themselves from that knowledge and their experiments.
Because I saw a foolish and inexperienced physician who had incised an abscess scrophilos in the neck of a woman, and incised some arteries of the neck so that great blood flowed while the woman died among the hands of him.
And I saw another physician who prescribed that the patient swallow a stone from a man who had processed in his state, and the stone was large, and it came to him and extracted that stone with a piece of the bladder, for that man on the third day died.
And I have already been called to extract that, and I saw that for the size of the stone and for the disposition of the patient I knew above him that he would die.
And I saw another physician who was taking a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and he came to a black man who was broken in his hip; and prepared the physician with his ignorance, extracted the fracture, over the wound, with splints and splints with strong structure, and did not leave the wound to breathe.
And then he let him go according to his desires, and he relieved him, and left him for a few days and commanded that we untie the ligament; and it was thus that the hip and the leg became infected with abscesses, and it came to ruin.
And I was called to him, and I appeared to untie the ligament, and achieved the tranquility and then eased his pains.
But however, the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, for I could not restrain it, and it did not cease to wander the corruption in the limb until the patient perished.
And I saw another physician who perforated a cancerous abscess, and it became ulcerated after a few days, until the malignancy of it was magnified to its lord.
The cause of which is that the cancer is pure of melancholic humor, therefore it does not come to it with iron at all, but that it be in a limb which suffers that it be entirely held hostage.
And therefore, sons, it is necessary for you that the operation with me be devised into two divisions: so it is in operation to which health is associated, and in work with which there is peril in the major dispositions.
And I have already existed that in all places of this book in which I see operation in which there is error and fear; because it is necessary for you to guard that and leave that, so that the fools do not find a way to speak and to dishonor you.
And therefore, take your weapons with diligence and protection of God, and your patients with facility and firmness.
And use the best way by the grace of God, seeking health and praiseworthy success, and leave the diseases terrible of difficult healing, and hold your weapons from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation in your faith and in your name does not escape you: because more is remaining to your glory, and more in the world and in the end to your sanctities.
Gualia already said in some of his admonitions: “Do not medicate bad sickness, so that bad physicians you are not called.”
And I have already divided this book according to three chapters.
This treatise begins the division of the book, and the first of the first part. The first chapter is ordered about the feet, in the forms of the instruments and in the tools of the cauteries, and of what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, of suction and perforation, and of leeches, and of poultices, and of the extraction of arrows and of things similar to those, all chaptered and ordered by the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter, of restoration and dislocation, and of the cure of sprains and of things similar to those; chapter ordered about the feet, and of the forms of the instruments.
Know that you should say the quality of the judgments of that cautery and of its harm, and in what completion it should be prohibited cautery.
Therefore I say that the sermon of the quality of the judgment of cautery and of its harm is a long and prolix sermon, and subtle by science, and secret hidden; and already many wise men have spoken of it, and they have disagreed about it, and to me a little of their sermons suffice, fearing prolixity.
And therefore I say that cautery conforms to every universal completion, whether it is of matter or of its matter, except for two complections, which are complections of cold matter.
In the cold and dry completion of matter, they disagree; for some say that cautery is beneficial to that, and others say the contrary, that cautery is not convenient in illness which is by quality and by dryness, because the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inconvenient that cold and dry illness with that which is hot and dry be healed.
And he who says the contrary of that, says that cautery is done beneficial in all cold and dry illness that comes in the bodies of men, because when you compare the body of man and its humors to the completion of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I say by the sermon of that, that experience has already to me on some occasions discovered.
But however, it should not come upon this that which is already explored and exercised in the chapter of cautery by the previous exercise, and who has known the diversity of the complexion of men and the disposition of the illnesses in their own bodies, and the causes of those, and their accidents, and the space of time of those.
But in the other complections, there is no fear upon you, and more so in the hot and humid illnesses, because all the physicians have agreed upon those, and they are not disagreed about the judgment with cautery in those.
And know, sons, that of the secret of cure by cautery with fire and of its goodness, it is because fire is simple, the action of which does not reach beyond the member which is cauterized and not to the other member attached to it, except with slight harm.
But the action of comburent medicine reaches to that in the members which are removed from it, and it makes them come to the member illness of difficult healing and often a great deal of harm.
But fire, by its sublimity and by the goodness of its substance, does not do this except that it superfluously. And it is already known to us by experience and by the length of service of study in the art about the truth of the causes; and for that reason I am excused from the length of the sermon, and if it were not that it is not written in my book in this place to you, a secret hidden with fire, and the quality of its operation in the bodies and of its expulsion by which it expels the illnesses, with a philosophical sermon demonstrative, which would be acute in your minds.
And know, sons, that they disagree about the time in which it is convenient to do cautery and pause the best time of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, because so that the harm by the accidental time is submerged in the goodness of that which with the cautery is thrown, and more so if the cautery is for pains or of necessary pains, strong and fistulas, which do not suffer tardiness because it is feared of those that come evil, which is greater than slight harm entering by time.
And thus do not catch in your minds, o sons, this that is not esteemed but by the vulgar people and the foolish physicians, so it is that to that illness which is healed by cautery is not reduced at all times, and they pause that consequence.
And the cause is not at all so as they think about it, because cautery is not but in place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries the humors which are the cause for which the pains come.
But however, cautery superfluously over medicine by the desire of its validity and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that its illness returns at some time in the future, according to the complexion of the patient and the location of its illness, and the virtue of it, and what is prepared in the body of it of the aggregation of the superfluities in it, and what has come to it in its acquisition in foods and things similar to those causes; unless that illness in which cautery was administered is a subtle illness in a member of few superfluities and humors, as cautery of the tooth for pain and things similar to it, it is possible that in it it does not return that pain, but rather that it is made in small.
And most common opinion is that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is a right opinion, for those who understand it in it, because they believe that there is no cure that profits with medicine nor with any other cause except cautery.
And the cause is the contrary; and the understanding that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is only when they administer the ways of cure in some diseases, and those medicines do not confer, and then at the end of the cause one administers cautery, and it profits for that. And therefore, that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, it is not according to the understanding which understand the common people and many of the foolish doctors.
And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance.
And they said that the place of cautery does not make a scar, as it is not absolutely true, because I have already seen that and have found that it does not do that except in some bodies, and cautery with that is good and better than with iron as they said; however, when you do cautery with fire with gold, it is not declared to you, because it is ignited according to the quantity that you want for the heat of the gold, and that it prepares to receive the heat; and if you adjust on it fire, the gold melts for the fire, and in the fire some plates so that the artisan catches for the occupation of that.
And for that reason cautery with iron must be done more lightly and more properly to the rectitude of operation.
And I have already ordered this chapter on cautery according to chapters, and I have ordered those of the head among the feet, so that afterward the one asking for that wants it.
The first chapter.
This cauterization confers on the humidity and coldness over the service accident of which there are two causes, so it is the cause of soda and multitude of flux rheumatic, called corissa, from the head to the parts of the ears and of the ears flowing, and multitude of sleep, and pain of teeth and of the throat, and universally of all illness that comes from coldness, as well as paralytically, soda and apoplexy, and similar in those illnesses.
The form of this cauterization is this, that first you command the patient to be evacuated with laxative medicine the head modifying, for three or for four nights, according to what requires the virtue of the illness and the age of him and his custom.
And then command him to shave his head, and then do that seizure between your hands on a low bench and that he place his hands on his feet.
And then place the razor of your palm near the nose between his heels. But however, as the your saying of the middle place is reached, sign that place with a tent, and then ignite the cautery olive of which this is the form:
And then place that on the place signed with a tent, in the manner that descends, with which your hand is constricted little by little, and you turn that.
And then lift your hand slightly and look at the place, and if you see already of the bone being discovered some quantity of the head, as well as the quantity of a grain of errs, then elevate your hand, and if not, turn your hand with that iron, with another of that, if it is cooled, until it is seen of the bone that I have told you.
And then take a little salt and dissolve that on the place and leave that for three days.
And then place on it a cloth soaked in butter and leave that on it until the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then cure the place with anguent tetrafarmacon until it is healed.
And already they said that when the plague remains open, so much better gets the scar, because it is better and more helpful.
And they said some of them that it should be cauterized the bone inside the bone, and it should be held the cautery until it is burned some part of the appearance of the bone.
And then be ras that which is burned of the bone, and then be cured.
And they said others that with the cautery reach the end, until it presses in the bone strong pressure until the bone breaks, and this is the form of alphecati small: And they estimate of that place expire the vapors of the head.
And it should be held the wound open for a long time, and then be cured until it is consolidated.
But to me no have been seen these two species of cautery of all, but in some men according to way of fear; and leave that, of me, better is with health, when it is; because the head is revealed for solution of continuity of it as well as we have testified in the other members, and more when the head of the patient is of cold nature.
And the species of cautery first is more safe and better of me; and of that husi and with that work with health.
Second chapter.
Of the cautery of the head.
When throughout the head occurs chronic and long pain and this is prolonged in the patient, and uses of herbs and of potions and of purgatives and of plasters and of guats and of cadels and of gualinas and of resemblances, and mostly if already is cauterized with a cautery which is counted and does not profit to him of any of those causes, then consider that if the head of the patient is of strong creation in its nature; and is not frail and finds a great cold, then cauterize with another cautery besides that one a little. And then cauterize that one on the corner of his head with a cautery until the bone is parted. Incise the bone and be discovered of the bone the quantity which we have recounted and cauterize that one with a cautery in the rear part of the head in the place which is called vas, — and is that place in which is placed a cupping glass. And alleviate your hand in that, and do not uncover the bone, because the patient by that finds a great pain different from the pain of all the other cauterizations of the head.
And you say this cautery in its place, because whoever the cautery with which are cauterized the horns of the head and the occiput is more subtle cautery than that with which is cauterized the middle place of the head; and this is the form of it.
Chapter Three.
Of cauterization of migraine non-ancient.
When in the part of the head pain is sudden, or is stretched pain into the eye, be evacuated with medicines the head modifying, and be administered the other cure, which I have said in the divisions of the sicknesses; and all does not profit, then cauterization in it is in two manners: or cauterization with medicine acute comburent, or with iron.
May cauterize with comburent medicine is that you take a handful of alum, and scour that and abcise the extremities of it from both the heads. And then incise the place of the pain in the temple with a lancet laid until there is in it made place besides the bone, until it is hidden.
And then strengthen over it with a stopped by descent constriction, and leave that for the spaces of three hours; and then untie the and take out the alum, and leave the plague for two or for three days, and then place over it a cloth submerged in water until the place makes a scab.
And then cure that with an enema until it is healed.
And if you want, do this with some comburent medicines which I have written in the two treatises of comburent medicines.
But the cauterization with iron according to this manner: ignite a cautery of which this is the form:
and it is called a clavilh, because the head of it is as the form of a clove in which there is some curvature, and in the middle place of it is a small eminence.
And then place over the place of the pain, and retain your hand — so that the artery which is besides — is not injured, and revolve the iron little by little with velocity.
And if the quantity of it that is cauterized by the thickness of the bone as much as the majority of it, and elevate your hand so that the artery which is besides is not injured, so that no blood comes.
And then imbibe a cloth in salt water and place that over the place, and leave that for three days; and then place a cloth mulled with water, and then cure with an enema until it is healed.
And if you want, cauterize with the extremity of the scalpel according to cautery, and guard yourself of incision of artery in this migraine properly non-ancient.
Chapter Four.
Of cauterization of ancient migraine.
When you cure migraine with that which we have said of the previous cure, and that which we have said in the divisions of the sicknesses, and it does not profit the cure, and sometimes by the sickness that does not reach to him that which we have said of the first cauterization with medicine or the cauterization with fire, then cover that you ignite the scalpel cautery until it is white, because it signifies over the place of the pain with a line of length of which is the majority of the said, or that which it is; and detain your hand for one time and strengthen that until you incise the artery and it arrives until the bone.
However necessary is to you that you guard of the continuation of the mandible, which is bad of the chewing, and that the lacert is not cauterized and the nerve which harms that, and that it does not become spasm.
And if it is about the custody and caution of the flow of blood from the artery that is incised, because in the incision of it there is fear, and mostly to him who ignores that which is done and is not studious and expert; and leave the operation in him at the beginning.
And I will come with remembrance of the regiment of the flow of blood accident of the artery according to its manner, in its place of this book.
And if you see of this sickness that does not suffice this cauterization and you see the body of the patient tolerable, cauterize that in the middle place of the head as we have recounted, and cure the plague until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cautery which we have mentioned in the chapter of the artery's cauterization, using a cautery with two handles, and this is a better cauterization and more convenient.
Chapter 5.
Of cauterization of ear pains.
When in the ear there is pain due to heat and it is cured with laxative causes and with the other cure which I have mentioned in the division, and the pain is not relieved, then ignite the cautery, and this is the one that has a point, of which this is the form:
And when it is pointed, ignite it, and it should be moved around the entire ear as a wheel is rolled, or in the circuit of whichever part if the pain is in whichever. Lengthen it with the cautery from the base of the ear little by little so that you can feel the place with your touch.
And if the cautery touches ten points in the entire ear, and that one, and then cure the places while they are healing.
Chapter 6.
Of cauterization of a tumor.
A tumor which is cured and by cauterization is only of the kinds which come from phlegm, according to what we have said in the divisions of the illnesses.
Avoid cauterization of the species that arises from dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you cure that species of tumor with poultices and purgatives and washes, and if you do not find your cure effective, then you must cauterize the tumor with three cauteries: the first you should apply to the base of the ear, the second a little below the temple, and the third to the junction of the two lips.
And pause your cautery for the opposite side of the diseased area, because softening does not come except in the side that is healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize that with the cautery in the right of the extremity of the ear, more sovereign a little above the corner of the head, and in the temple another, the length of which should be according to the length of the finger, and pause your hand with the cautery until the quantity of the majority of the species of the code is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a species of the cutler, the form of which is shown in front. But however more subtle it is that one a little so as you see; and where a handle in it instead of superfluous thickness a little.
And then cure the place with that which is shown in front until it is healed.
Chapter 7.
Of cauterization of old apoplexy.
When apoplexy is old and you cure that with the water which we have said and if you do not find your medication effective and the illness does not have fever, then cauterize that with four cauteries: on top of all the horns of its head; and with cautery and the middle part of the head, as we have said; and with cautery in the nape of the neck. And the manner of the cautery is made according to what has been said before.
And it is already cauterized above the mouth of the stomach; and it is more posterior; and then it should be cured with the water that proceeds.
Chapter 8.
Of cauterization of oblivion made by flame.
And when it is given to the patient at the beginning, large poultices and pills of the serving modifying.
And then shave the head of the patient and place on the nape of his neck a plaster of the kind described in the treatise of plasters.
And pause that several times, for that is the manner of cauterizing. And do water according to that same order which I have already said.
And therefore if by those it is healed well; and if not, then make to him three cauteries in the rear part of his head, which should be descending from the most sovereign part of the head into the part most below the neck. And pause between each cautery the thickness of the finger, and then cure the cautery with the water that proceeds.
But if you add more and the illness is water-tolerant, then make to him cauteries in the middle place; and if you wish for greater addition, then cauterize that on the two horns.
And then cure that until it is healed; and let the cautery be olive according to the form given before.
Chapter 9.
Of cauterization of paralysis and of softening of the whole body.
And that you proceed in softening of the head with poultices and with the water which we have said; and then shave the head of the patient, and then cauterize that with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery on top of all the horns of the head, and with a cautery on the rear part of him, and with three cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck.
And if it is necessary in the illness of softening of the body of too much and the illnesses tolerant and the illness is strong, then cauterize that with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the loins, and diligently with a cautery until it is burned of the code of him, and raise your hand. And then take care of the one who is being healed, and this one should be an olive cautery.
Chapter X.
Of cauterization of epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, but only if the epilepsy is due to phlegm.
And therefore, if you modify the brain of him at the beginning of him with years and with the other cure which we have said in the division when the patient is great and is tolerating the excess of medicines.
And if it is a child who does not suffer the medicines, then administer safeguards and masticators to the brain, before that for several days, with the blessing of the food.
And then shave the head of the patient, and then cauterize him with a cautery in the middle location of the head according to the previous manner, and with another cautery in the back of his head, and on each horn of his head cauterize. And if the patient is strong and is tolerating, then cauterize him with cauteries the ones which I have said, having paralysis and softening of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back.
And be an olive cautery according to what is preceded.
But if the patient is a child, then pause a subtle cautery according to this manner.
Chapter XI.
Of cauterization of melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are humidities corrupted and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries which we have said in the having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is superfluity declining to melancholy, and the body of the patient is humid, then give him to drink water that purifies his brain according to what has preceded in the division.
And then shave the head of the patient, and then make a decent tortoise of him on the circle, and then place that in the middle location of the head.
And the patient be feeling cauterized, and be held from all sides.
And then apply liniment; and it is more worthy to border with sheep's wool. And warm that over the fire for a moderate heating by measure, the one which the said suffers when it is most in him. And then put that in the middle location of his head in the circle, and leave him until it is cooled.
And do this water with the patient every week once, with the other regimen of him good while he is being healed; or if you want, cauterize this by making small points according to the most of him, unless you have the hand with a cautery so ordered: this is a special kind of cautery which moistens the brain with equality.
And then place that coat embedded in wool or in  gualina's  grays.
Chapter XII.
Of cauterization of  water descending in the  womb.
When to you is declared the beginning of water in the womb by the signs which I have said in the division, then begin and give to the patient to drink water that purifies his head, and guard him from all humidities.
And make that suffer in a bath in degu for some days.
And then command him to shave his head, and cauterize that with a cautery in the middle location of the head; and then cauterize that with two cauteries on two temples if it is the beginning of the descent of water in two wombs, or of one side if it is the beginning of the water in one womb.
Incise with cautery all the veins and arteries which are left the  codena; and be the cauteries in that length in the latitude of the temples.
And guard yourself from fluxes of blood when it is cauterized; and if you see from him fluxes of blood, stop him with some medicine, the one which is to you possible.
And you will come with wisdom the one which is in the extraction of arteries and in the abscess of those and caution of fluxes of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized in the neck below two bones with two cauteries deliberately produced.
Chapter XIII.
Of cauterization of old tears.
When tears from the wombs are old and by the veins and arteries which are in the manifest location of the head outside and it is verified that this is superfluous frigid phlegmatic, then cauterize that with the cautery which we have recounted in the chapter of the beginning of water descending in the wombs, and with a cautery in the middle location of the head and with two cauteries in the neck below two temples, and with two cauteries in the neck below two bones. And if you are indigested of addition, then cauterize that in all the side of the tail of the womb on the extremity of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Chapter XIV.
Of cauterization of nose odor.
When you medicate him with the water which we have said in the division and it does not profit your medication, then you equip and give to the patient the cochies for three nights; and then shave the head of him, and cauterize him with a middle cautery with an olive cautery. And then cauterize that with a pointed cautery, with two cauteries on the two eyebrows, leaving the hair a little.
And guard yourself from the archery that you do not burn that.
And of the pointed cautery this is the form.
Chapter .xv.
Of cautery for softening eyelids of the eyes.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by illness or by humidity, then cauterize that eyelid with a cautery with this lunar cautery; and this is the form of it:
And if you, cauterize that above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries in all parts, and be elongated from the temples. And let the length of each cautery be according to the quantity of the eyebrow.
And do not press too hard your hand with the cautery, but according to the quantity that the third part of the eyelid be cauterized.
Chapter .xvi.
Of cautery of the eyelid of the eye when the hairs are converted to the parts of the inside and punch the eye.
When the hairs of the eye are converted to the parts of the inside so that they puncture the eye, cauterize in those in two manners, either cauterize or is with burning medicine.
If with cautery of it with fire, command the patient in front of it that he see his hairs as those which they cleanse, until they are prolonged and lengthened; and if he punches that, then you strengthen the eyes of him with a bandage so that it is not harmful until the hairs are born.
Therefore, as soon as they are born and lengthened, then pause the head of the patient in your seat, and then send over the eyelid of his eyes with a tent, with a sign which is according to the figure of a myrtle leaf, and be the beginning of the sign near the hairs.
And then place a poultice buried in a white of egg or in a mucilage of ptilli over the eye.
And then ignite the cautery of which this is the form of it.
And then cauterize over the figure which you have marked, little by little, in several times, until the surface of the  code is burned, which is as a myrtle leaf, all apparent properly.
And sign of health of your work is that you see the eyelid of the eye already be contracted and the hairs of it be elevated from the puncture of the eye.
And therefore elevate your hand and leave it for three days, and then place over it a poultice with border until the scab is eradicated. And then cure it with an enema until it is healed.
But if it returns for the hairs any cause to their puncture and the eyelid is softened, then do another time the cautery over that all as you had done first.
But if the hairs are in the eyelid, then cauterize it until it is elevated to its natural place and is lengthened and that the hairs do not puncture the eye.
But the cautery with burning medicine this is that you command the patient that he see the hairs until they are prolonged and lengthened, and then be made of cloth the form of a myrtle leaf.
And then take of known soap and of living cause one. i., that is,
And place the said over the medicine and press it a little and do not harm until the patient feels the bite of the medicine, for bite is in it as of fire.
And therefore as it will endure that the other bite, then remove the medicine and put it with your hand; therefore as it ceases the bite, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water; and then consider if times the eyelid is already lifted as it is washed from the constriction with fire or with incision, for then it is well; and if not return over it of the medicine over the place in which it has not put the medicine and do not degrade until it is lengthened your operation and be contracted the eye.
And then place over it a poultice with border until the scab of the burning is eradicated, and then cure it with an enema of  a definite or with another until it is healed.
And it is necessary to you,  in your operation that you guard with great diligence that in the eye does not fall any of the medicine, and if the eyelid almost some days is softened and for any cause the hairs puncture the eye, then iterate your medicine over that place which of the eyelid is softened, and properly as you had done at the beginning, and then encircle it until it is healed.
And this is the form of a myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men are diversified according to the magnitude and the smallness, and therefore according to that is made your constriction.
And the path of rectum should not be hidden from him who studies this art.
Chapter XVII.
Of cauterization of fistula that is in the lacrimal of the heel.
When you cure a fistula with what we have said in the divisions of diseases and do not confer your cure, then you must cauterize it according to this manner: command the patient to place his head on your lap, and hold the head of him some minister between your hands in such a manner that it is not disturbed nor agitated with his head.
And then place a cloth soaked in oil or in a poultice of ptilli on the heel of him.
And then ignite the cautery of which this is the form:
Which is concave, as is the shape of a cane or a vulture's feather, from one extremity of which the cautery is made.

Chapter XXI.
Of cauterizing tooth pain.
When tooth pain is due to coldness, or there is a worm in it, or it does not respond to cure with medicine, then cauterization is done in that tooth in two ways: cauterization with a cow's horn, or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with horn is that you take the horn of a cow and heat it in a blacksmith's forge, and then take a handle and wrap it around the tip of the horn, and then immerse that in the heated horn, and place it on the painful tooth firmly while it is heated.
And then repeat this several times until the power of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge wool or a stick in the heated horn above, and place it on the painful tooth, and place a red-hot iron on top of it until the iron reaches the bottom of the cavity of the tooth.
But however, cauterization with fire is that you attend to the handle of the iron or of the cautery, and that it is in the middle of it some thickness and the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And then ignite the cautery, the shape of which will come, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand over it while the cautery is heated; and do this several times because the pain will be mitigated either on that day or the next day.
And cover that by the pressure of that cautery the patient rinses his mouth with good broth and keeps it there for an hour and then spits it out; and this is the shape of the cautery.
And cauterize with whichever extremity you wish according to what is possible for you.
And this is the shape of the cannula:

When joint pain is caused by cold humors that infiltrate each part of the body, and pain occurs in the feet, it is customarily called gout by doctors.
And therefore, as gout caused by cold is cured by a method of cure and not only the pains are removed, then the pains are removed by cauterization.
And it is that you cauterize that after evacuation in the circuit of the joint of the foot with many cauteries.
And let it be an olive cautery of which this is the form of it:
And if it is necessary to make points on the surface of the foot, then do so with a pointed cautery. And if the pains rise into the knees or to the other joints, and this many times happens, then cauterize that over each knee with three cauteries or four of the entire part with this olive cautery.
And if many cauteries that these cauteries are necessary to you, then cauterize that and do not press too much your hand with the cautery before, be only around the circumference of the bone.
And if the pains rise into the knee and the back, then administer the cautery which we have said in its chapter.
And if the pains are in the hands only, and it is called suagra, then point in the circuit of the knuckles as they revolve, point in those two lines.
And if the pains remain in the fingers, then point in the circuit of the knuckles over each node and over the palm of the hand.
And if the pains rise near the bones to the elbows or to the muscles, then cauterize the ones of the entire part of the armpits.
And do not evacuate the patient of good regimen and reception of medicines, because if it is done good regimen and it is evacuated with this cautery it is healed, God help.

Chapter XLIX.
Of the cauterization of ulcers that are mortified.
When ulcers are old and do not respond to any of the medicinal treatments, then you cauterize over it with a cautery, a little, according to the amount of the depth of the flesh, until the whiteness and color of it are removed, and the color of it is changed.

Chapter L.
Of the cauterization of crabs.
When cancer begins and you want to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery around its perimeter, as it is turned.

Chapter LI.
Of the cauterization of boils.
When some boil is delayed in maturation, and so it is because of the superfluity that causes it, or because of the patient's age, because he is old and decrepit, of little blood, or because of time, and you want to hasten the maturation of the boil; then cauterize around it with small, moving cauteries, and then leave it so that it will hasten in maturation.
But if you want the perforation of it with a cautery, then you ignite the cautery, the form of which is this: and place it in the middle location of the boil until it penetrates the flesh.
And if the cautery in that location is deeper, so that the body of the arm is relieved; and then carefully treat it while it is healing.
Chapter LII.
Of the cauterization of corrodents.
Corrodent is a corruption that walks in the member, which corrodes it as a fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, if you see that corrodent in a location that suffers cauterization with fire, then you ignite small, moving cauteries, and large ones according to what is convenient in that location where the corrodent is.
And then cauterize it from all sides until you eradicate all the corrosion and no cause of it remains.
And then leave it for three days, and place on the cauterized areas a compress with oil mixed together until all the scars are eradicated and all the corruption.
And then treat it with poultices that generate flesh.
But if after three days you see that healthy flesh is born in which there is no corruption, well; but if not, then repeat the cautery over what is raw in the corrupted locations.
And corrodent is medicated some times with sharp medicine, which that is placed in place of cautery. But however, cauterization with fire is of more light help.
And I have already said the cure of it with sharp medicine in the division, and therefore take that when you have an emergency from it.
Chapter LIII.
Of the cauterization of warts and other similar ones.
Many times, a malady called a wart appears on the lower parts of the foot, and it is a large, thick, growth which disfigures the foot; and it is cauterized in those in two ways, either with fire cautery or with boiling water cautery.
But the fire cautery is that you ignite the concave cautery, resembling the beak of a vulture, which should be made of iron according to the size that contains the wart from all sides, and be of subtle margins.
And then place that ignited one on the wart, and then revolve your hand with the cautery around the circuit of the wart until the cautery reaches the depth of the wart. And let him rest for three days before he begins to raise his arm. Then apply a plaster made of wild herbs crushed with salt, and leave the plaster on it for a night, for this will be eradicated from its roots.
And then cure the area with an enema of generative flesh until it is healed.
And if it is not converted, and many times this happens on the surface of the body, mostly in the hands and feet, then you should administer cautery to those with water, and you should take a cannula of lead or iron or vulture's bone, and place it on the claw; and then pour a small quantity of water into the cannula, and hold your hand, and you revolve that with compression of your hand of all, and press the edge of the cannula into the root of the claw, and it will drive the water cauda via to the root of the claw; and wait for the patient a little the bite of the water cauda for an hour, and then remove it, for the claw with its roots will be eradicated.
And thus do to those, and the other one until you come upon all of them on their body.
And then cure those pus that the roots of the claws are eradicated with this of the enemas which the flesh generates.

But the manner of acting on it is that you make the patient lie on the prepared and straight saddle, and then take its head in your two hands and pull it so that you see the swelling coming to the lower parts, and then let it dry and not descend, and keep the light, and the patient sees the causes as you see.

But if the descent is not prepared to the swelling with the water that we have said, then make the patient lie between your hands and then take a fine spatula and cut into it on the panniculus, separating a little of the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea in the crown (in the place where the eye is), until the swelling is removed.
Therefore, when it is removed, then you distill into the wound water cauda in which you have mixed honey or water in which you have already boiled fennel and honey.
And then cure it with the other causes until it is healed.
Chapter XXII.
Of the cure of the descending water of the wound.
We have already said the species of water in the division and which one it is convenient to pierce with a sermon, declaring it according to the health.
Now, it is necessary that you make the patient lie between your hands on a chair and tie their wound tightly.
And then place your left hand near the eyelid of their eye, if the eye in which the water is the left eye; or on your right hand, if the eye is the right.
And then with your right hand take the almond, if the eye is left; or with your left hand, if the eye is right.
And then place the tip of the almond near the crown for the thickness of the ray in the album of the eye from the side of the lacrimal gland, and then press the almond with virtue and roll your hand with it.
And then penetrate into the album of the eye and feel that the almond has already reached the cause of the void.
And it is necessary that the measure of the path of the almond to the root is the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackness, and it is the crown of the eye; because you will see with it the pupil with the vision of the eye through the clarity of the tunic cornea.
And then place the almond into the place where the water is, and then you throw it down once, then another, and therefore if the water descends immediately, then wet the patient's wound with water over which he will look immediately, and the almond in their eye.
And then rest for a little; therefore if the water has descended, then you remove that other time as long as the almond is not thrown away.
And therefore when it is dried and does not descend, then you extract the almond with ease, and roll it with your hand little by little, and then dissolve in the water a little clear salt of gemma and with that wash the eye carefully; and then place outside the eye cotton or stopper or wool soaked in rose oil and egg white and lubricate the eye with water.
But in those who are of our time, place on that with a tripe soaked in egg white.
And if you do not obey your almond to the entrance of the eye because of its hardness — because it is in some men whose eye is very hard — then it is necessary that you take the spatula which is called alberid of which this is the form:
And therefore pierce with it that conjunctiva, and do not end your hand in the track, and it is not if you do not make a path for the almond to go in subtly.
And then, insert the almond according to what we have said.
And you must complete the work, prepare the patient to sleep soundly in a dark room, lying on his back, and prohibit all movements.
And pause in his nature so that it may be cleansed, and do not turn his head to the right or left at all.
And let the bandage be according to its disposition on the third day.
And then, untie that in that dark room and remove the eye cover, and make him see some causes, and then return the bandage on the seventh day.
And do not cover that which you have done in the hour of cures or as soon as the infusion. Have it covered so that your water may flow lightly through great and vehement regard.
But if pus should occur, then you must untie the bandage before the seventh day, and rectify that with the water that yields pus.
Then you must remove the cover from his eyes and place your hand over his face through which the movement of him is governed, leaving him for a few days, existing in the dark room.
And then, he must be taken out of that room gradually and converse about his causes.
And know that in alchemy, the disciple of vision is not excused some times, and then you should be bold about the operation.
And now we have come to some of those who are in the Artach, and some said that they made fire in the Ayrac magdaam perforated with which the water is sucked.
But however, I have not seen any in our land who had perfect water, nor is water mentioned in some of the books of the ancients; and it is possible that this is novel.
And these are the forms of the species of magdaan so that it may be upon those who ignore those:
And they are made of iron or properly of iron, and their extremities are with this triangular subtlety, the acute extremity as such is the form.
Chapter XXIV.
Of the cure of flesh wounds in the nose.
When in the nose are born diverse carns adjusted of which some cause is assembled to a scorpion of motz pes, or to a polyp peys; and this malady is called polyp because it is similar to that peys represented. And of this is cancerous flesh, lapadea, of dusky color; and of this is that flesh leon not of dusky color.
Therefore, in that which is in these flesh leon not fraudulent nor cancerous, you must make the patient sit between your hands and placed in the sun, and open his nostrils, and pierce your own onci in those carns. And then extract that to the foreparts, and then incise that which you have comprehended of those with a sharp subtle spatula of one part, so that you know that all the flesh is already removed; that if any cause of it remains, of which the abscission is possible, then you root that with one of the subtle instruments with ease so that nothing of it remains. But if it bleeds or pus should occur, then you pause to him that which you should; or if it is of the malignant abscesses, then you cut and cauterize that so that it may be abscindit sanc and the cavities are all removed.
And then be getatz in the nose after the incision vi agre and water or wine. But if the nose is open and from it proceeds humidity into the palate, then you know that it is already healed.
But if the humidity does not penetrate as it should, then you know that from it the flesh wounds in the pus sobiras bones of the nose to which the abscission has not reached.
Therefore, then you must introduce a thread of linen into which there is some thickness, and nudge in it moth nuts, and place between each nut the quantity of the finger or less, and engage the patient and introduce one extremity of the thread into the nose with the ray or with another cause which is to it possible.
And as that will have done, that it may cast its odor into that which reaches the canals of the nose, and be spit upon the patient's throat, for troops of times the semblance to this action do the children at the schools, and it is lighter cause to him who wants to do it.
And then place the two extremities of the thread, one extremity that escapes over the nose and the other that remains in the nose, and then administer a lock of flesh with the nuts that are in the thread, and do this so that you know that the flesh is already with the nuts of the thread.
And then extract the thread, and place in the nose after the abstraction of the blood a poultice, and do this for three days or more until the engent corroded all that which is remains of the flesh.
And then at the end of the cause, place in the nose a tube of lead for some days until it is healed.
But if in the course of the cure that requires, use of that.
And this is the form of the instrument a capipurge maker with which oils and medicines are distilled in the nose:
And make a plate of silver or brass, which is like a small open lamp, thus as a small basin, and the meat seemingly.
And if you wish, make a closed tube like a cane, and the nozzle of the instrument to be a maker of purging and be flat, uncovered; to which there is a handle at the back of it, with which you have that when you heat it in oil or water that you want of the suckable juices and causes.
Chapter XXV.
Of the nats in the extremities of the nose.
Many times the nat is seen in the extremities of the nose, and it is magnified and noted on some days when it is not seen.
And for that cove that you notice that at the beginning of the appearance of it, and record all of that. And then place over the area the cautery or medicine comburent the which was in place of it.
But if it is late its incision before it is magnified, then consider if it is calcified, hard, of dark color and of little feeling, then do not touch that with iron because it is a purulent abscess; because many times to the one who incides this abscess it befalls great malice upon the one who had it.
And if the abscess is of lion touching and not of dark color, and times that incision is possible in all of it, then evacuate the patient and incisions that without fear, and cure the place with water that excises and constrict within that it be healed.
Chapter XXVI.
Of suturing of the nose and of the lips and of the ear when continuity is dissolved by plague or by resemblances.
Know that when accidents dissolution of continuity in one of these cartilages, little confer you in that operation unless in some men.
Therefore, when it befalls to any cause of those, that you consider if it is fresh plague with its blood, and then you adjust the two lips of the plague with suture, and then cure that until it be healed.
And if the lips of dissolution of continuity are already separated, and each is made healthy, then it behooves you to excoriate each part of its apparent codena until blood comes out. And then adjust the two lips with suture and strengthen those, and on those pulverize blood of dragon and incense, and place over the powder a patch of diaphicon plaster, or of some other of the consolidating plasters, and leave that tied for two days or three, and then untie that and change that plaster and leave that until the fibers be by themselves abscinditz, and then cure with enguent until it be healed.
But the manner of the suture is that you add the dissolution of continuity or with needles as we have recounted in the suture of the belly, or add the dissolution of continuity with thread as to you and have made known.
Chapter XXVII.
Of extraction of those causes that come in the two lips in the parts between.
Many times it befalls to many men in the parts between of their lips some abscesses hard resembling to fat of worms, and some of them are smaller and some are larger.
Therefore, it behooves you to convert the lips and fendas each of those hardnesses from all parts, and then the abscesses you fill the place of sage incense until the blood be restrained, and then be washed with wine and be cured the place with water that is styptic, until it be healed.
Chapter XXVIII.
Of incision of the flesh adjusted in the gums.
Great many times there is on the gum flesh adjusted the which the ancients called albulus, therefore it behooves you to suspend that with an ounce or that you have that with the forceps and incisions that you must the root, and leave the sania to run or the blood.
And then place over the place sage incense or other powders styptic or excicative.
And if that flesh returns, then incisions that secondarily, and cauterize that, for then the cautery will not return.
Chapter XXIX.
Of reason of teeth with iron.
When on the surface of the teeth of the parts between and of the front and between the gums are adjusted scabs rough, white, and some times are of nigras and are made citrinas or green until the gums come by that corruption and are made the teeth white.

Therefore, if this is what is at the beginning of the reason, it is good; and if not, then you repeat the reason on those the other day and the second and the third until it comes to the last statement in what you want.
And know that the teeth have need of diverse forms and figures of instruments according to how it is prepared for your operation. Chapter .xxx.
Of the Extraction of Teeth.
Take care that you cure the tooth of its pain with all care and take your time in its entire extraction, for there is no cause that should supplant the healing of it when it is extracted, for it is substance sublimated within that the excuse in the extraction of it.
But take care when the patient is forced to have that tooth extracted, that you firmly ascertain which is the aching tooth, for many times the pain deceives the patient and leads you to believe it is in a healthy tooth, and you extract that one and the pain does not cease until the bad and aching tooth is extracted, for we have already seen this by the operation of the barbers.
Therefore, as you must ascertain which is the aching tooth, and that you know well, then you must scarify in the circuit of the tooth with a spatula in which there is some virtue, until it is dissolved from the tooth of the gums of all parts, and then make that with your fingers, or with subtle forceps at the beginning little by little until you make it come loose.
And after that, firmly hold it with large pliers for good communication or strong stupor, and place the head of the patient between your teeth, which you well hold that it does not harm, and then pull the tooth according to rectitude in a manner that you do not break it, nor give the patient greater pain.
And therefore, if it is not forgotten, then take one of those instruments, and place that behind it of all parts with facility and exert the removal of it as it was done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is broken or corroded, then you must compresses of cloth that break and tighten that with the extremity of a fine ray so that it is not broken in the hour of your constriction upon it with pliers.
And you must operate exquisitely with scarification in the circuit of all parts of the gums and guard much your strength that you do not break it and remain a part of it, and return upon the patient by the malice that be greater than the first pain of it.
And guard yourself that you do not do what some ignorant barbers do in their fumbling and audacity about the extraction of teeth, since they do not administer what we have recommended; for many times they bring upon men illnesses great ones that are more difficult to be cured, and the roots of them remaugulated all, or some of those, or that you extract that with some bones of the jaw as many times as we have witnessed.
And after the extraction of it, the mouth should be washed with wine caut or wine agre with salt.
And if it should flow of blood thereby, as many times it should, then triss some quantity of zegi and sprinkle it upon the wound, and if you do not confer that zegi, cauterize.
The form of the forceps and pliers subtle with which the tooth is pulled at the beginning be of long extremity, of short handle and thick, so that they are not bent when with those you must operate.
And be as many times of thick handle within that when you tighten with those they are not bent, be short extremities.
And be made of Indian iron, descentment made of straight extremities, and in the extremities of those be teeth of which some introne in the others and tighten by strong constriction descent, and some times the extremities of those be the form of the beak of a bird which has the name ciconia, so it is guanta, and are of strong constriction.
Chapter .xxxi.

Chapter .xxxii.
Of the cure of the prominent teeth over the others.
When the teeth are prominent not according to their natural course, for those the shape is laid, and mostly when it happens to women, and mostly to the venerable old ladies; therefore, since you consider: if a tooth is nothing near another tooth, and it is not possible to suture or liniment it, then eradicate that; but that it is not annexed to another tooth, then you incise that with this instrument of which this is the shape; and it is similar to a pig's snout, and be made of Indian iron of a sharp extremity.
And be your incision with which you incise that in too many days for the hardness of the tooth, and that it is not damaged another of the teeth.
And if the prominent tooth is exposed to filing, then file that with a file of Indian iron of which this is the shape:
And be all of Indian iron the margin and very well; and be of very small points as a file with which needles are made, with which the tooth be filed little by little in many days with facility, so that no other tooth be damaged and broken. And then line that at the end, and ratz that with some razors.
And if the tooth of which one part is stuck and it hinders the tongue, then when you file that until the sharpness of that fracture is stayed and smoothed, and be filled so that the tongue does not touch it and the word does not break.
Chapter .xxxiii.
Of restoration of damaged teeth with gold or silver filings.
When accidents happen to the teeth in front with concussion and removal by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot strengthen over that which manages, and you have cured that with topical medicines, and it has not been of any use, then for so that it does not break, it is generated in those that are strengthened with gold filings and not silver, because silver becomes green and soon you can see it, but gold at no time is changed.
And be the filings in such subtlety and thickness according to the quantity that can enter between the teeth; and the shape of the straight is that you take the filing and take double of it between two healthy teeth, and then that you increase with two tortuosities of the filing between two damaged, or if it is one or many, until it reaches the healthy tooth of the other part. And then iterate the testimony within the part of which you begin, and strengthen your hand with facility and wisdom so that it is not damaged.
And be your striccio with which you strengthen the filings, the roots of the teeth so that it does not escape.
And then incise the extremities of the superfluous filings with the forceps or tweezers, and add those in each place with care, and convert them and hide them between the healthy tooth and the damaged tooth, so that it does not cause injury to the tongue. And then leave that so straight as a Roman.
But if it is loosened or broken, strengthen that or those with another filing in such a manner in all its time.
And this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the rectification of two healthy teeth and two damaged, as well as sometimes these are tied:
And when it is done that a tooth or two are returned to their places after the falling of each one, and they are recreated as we have recounted, and that they remain damaged.
And that is done only by good artificers and wise.
And sometimes it is fitted some cause of the bones of cows, and it is made as such as the shape of a tooth, and it is placed in the place where the tooth is missing, and it is strengthened as we have said, and it remains and serves with that for a long time.
Chapter .xxxiv.
Of the incision of the ligament which comes in the tongue and prohibits speech.
This ligament which comes from under the tongue some times or is natural with which man is born, or accidental and caused by a plague which is already consolidated.
And the operation on it is that men open the mouth of the patient, his head existing in the tieu se; and elevate his tongue, and then incisions that ligament nerve according to the latitude so that it be dissolved the tongue from its recess.
But if in that there is any hardness or knotting, and this is due to the consolidation of a plague, then you throw an oil and split that by the latitude so that as you have incised the ligament and the knot is dissolved.
And guard yourself that no fissure be made in the flesh of the preon and that you split here artery and blood comes.
And then wash the vestiges of the incision with water or with wine vinegar or with hot water; and then place under the tongue linen; so is the method which holds the patient's tongue in each night so that it be not consolidated another time.
But if blood flow occurs, place on the location vitriol trissat; but if the blood comes, then cauterize the location with a lancet cauterizing the which convenes ad aquo. And then that cure with the other causes so that it be healed.
Chapter .xxxv.
Of the extraction of a ranula under the tongue.
Sometimes an abscess occurs under the tongue resembling a small lump which prohibits the tongue from its natural operation; and often it is magnified so that it swells the mouth.
And the operation on it is that men open the mouth of the patient, seeing before the sun and considers the abscess.
And if you see it of dark color or black, hard, to which the patient does not feel any sensation, then do not touch that, for it is gangrenous.
And if it is inclined to whiteness, in which there is moisture, then you put the oil in it, and incisions it with a subtle spatula, and incisions it from all parts; and if blood comes to you in the hour of your operation, then you place above it zegi trissat, that is vitriol, so that it be restricted the blood.
And then return to your work so that you have treated it with compliment of it, so that it be washed with wine vinegar and salt; and cure it with the other cure ad aquo so that it be healed.
Chapter .xxxvi.
Of the extraction of an abscess of the two ears and of that which is nothing in the goiter and of the other abscesses.
When in the goiter, it is swollen, so are the glands which are assembled swollen, which sometimes occur externally and are called two ears, which when you cure them with water that we have said in the division and it is not healed, then consider if the abscess is hard, of dark color, of little sensation, then do not touch that with iron.
And if it is of red color and the root is thick, then do not touch that with iron because of the flow of blood; let it lay there until it is matured, and then either you will extract it, or it will be broken by itself.
And if it is of white color, soft, and the root of it is subtle, then that is the one that must be incised.
And the operation on it is that you consider, before your operation, if the abscess of it has already rested, with a complete rest, or if it has diminished with any diminution; and then make the patient stand before the sun, and his head be in the tieu se, and open his mouth, and the servant takes between his hands, pressing the tongue of it from below with a noble instrument of which this is the form:

And other water that you pull some cause of the tunics, and then incise it with the instrument of which this is the form: And it is assembled like forceps, but the extremities of it are curved, so that the orifice of each one is in the straight of the other, very sharp, the one which is of iron indi embedded.

But if there is a flow of blood, wash with water of decoction of the bark of  millefolium or of myrtle leaf and similar to that of the stiptic causes so that the flow of blood be restricted, and then cure it so that it be healed.
And sometimes there are born in the goiter other abscesses other than those two ears, and incise those according to what I have said in the incision of two wells equally.
And I had once treated a woman with an abscess which was located in the throat of her, the abscess tended to a brownish color, of little feeling, the one which had already closed the throat of her, and the woman was breathing with tight meat, and had already prohibited her to eat and drink water, and she had already arrived at death if more a day or two.
And the abscess had already grown so much that it had meters two ramps inside which they came out through two tracts.
Therefore I cuitegui fisturally and I stayed in one of them openings, and I pulled out that one, and thrown is of it a great portion, and then I incised that one from where I understood of the other tract, and then I opened the mouth of it, and I compressed its tongue, and then I stayed the opening in that abscess.
And then I abscised a large portion of it, and it was not running from it but a little of blood. Therefore absolutely was the throat of that woman, and she began to drink water, and then she ate food, therefore I did not cease to incise that abscess many times for a long time, and it succeeded abscess in place of that one, the one which incision entered while it was prolonged that one.
Therefore I engineered a needle and cauterized the throat of her, therefore as much as addition; and then I walked around and I did not know what God had done of that then to me.
Chapter .xxxvii.
Of incision of a boil when it is an abscess.
When catarr arises in the boil, and it is an abscess and it is long, then it is called perpendicular; and if it is in the part below thick and round, and then it is called buba.

But if this instrument is not at your present, then take a cane and compose in the extremity of it a cup of wool, so that the mouth of the patient be covered, because the wool cup prohibits the vapor from burning the mouth.
And this cure is good for health.
Chapter .xxxviii.
Of the extraction of thorns and of what adheres in the throat and of the other causes.
Moistened things adhere in the throat or a thorn of fish or any other cause.
Therefore, it is necessary that you extract what of those appears, on which the sight falls, because you press the tongue with an instrument beforehand, so that to you it is declared what is in the throat.
And what does not appear and is to you hidden in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach, because often the cause annexed to the throat is thrown-out by vomit; or that the patient swallows a piece of bread or a root of lettuce or a mouthful of dry bread; or  chew a piece of dry marine sponge, and tie it firmly with a thread, and then the patient swallows it, because when it arrives at the place where the spines are and is extracted, then it is thrown-out. And more, take an eel and tie it firmly with a thread, and it is placed and gently extracted; or take a pear and gently the stem and gently the end.
But if it is not thrown-out with those causes which we have said, then use an instrument of lead according to this form:
And let it be thicker than a small ray, and in the extremity of it be a concavity which you introduce into its throat with ease.
And let him take his head elevated upwards, and be careful that the touching of his bone of the throat, so that it becomes engaged with his body and with that which pushes the bone or the thorn, or that the doctor with his hand.
But however, that the patient that introduces is best, by his knowledge of the place of the annexed cause and pushes down, and pulls his hand with the instrument upwards, all that according to the quantity which is prepared for him before it is thrown-out.
Chapter .xxxix.
Of the extraction of bloodsucker annexed to the throat.
When the bloodsucker is medicated with what we have said in the division of the cure with medicines and does not confer, consider then in the throat of the patient to the sun, because you have examined the tongue of him with an instrument which we have recommended to you.
Therefore, if you see the bloodsucker, extract it with a small pin or with a subtle gesture gently.
And if it is not possible to extract with that, then take a concave cannula and introduce it into the throat of the patient, and then place in the concavity of the cannula a burning iron, and do this so many times (until the bloodsucker is dead and is removed from the throat) and abstain the patient all day of water.
And then chew a full mouthful of cold water, and work the mouth of him in that, and wash the mouth with that; and do not swallow any of that, and bad the water an hour after another with his hand, because the bloodsucker as soon as it feels the water catz.
But if it is not thrown-out with what we have recommended, then fumigate the patient with cumin or with asafoetida with the instrument which we have recommended in the fumigation of the uvula.
Do this, so long as it falls.
And there is another way of operation in the fumigation of that, is that you take an olla in which there are burning coals and the olla be covered with a cover in the middle of which there is a trough, and it is composed in that trough the extremity of the instrument; and then let go downwards the fumigation; and place the patient his mouth at the extremity of the cannula, and close his mouth so that the fumigation is not thrown-out until you know that the fumigation has arrived at the bloodsucker, because the bloodsucker as soon as it falls.
And if it does not catch, then you repeat the fumigation many times, and abstain the patient from drinking, and eat salty and bitter causes, and do not drink water, and thus it is necessary that with this regimen it be thrown-out.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the bloodsucker of the throat is treated when it is seen; and it is similar to forceps as you see, unless that in it there is some curvature: which is placed in the throat, and the extremity of it is similar to the beak of a stork, which is smooth, in which it is sharpened with a file, so that, when it grips any cause, it does not let go.
Chapter .xl.
In which is the sum of the sermon on the opening of abscesses and their section.
Abscesses are special sores, of various kinds, according to the remembrance of them, of each one in this book.
And they are diverse in their perforation and section by two ways, of which one is by the nature of the abscesses themselves; and by that which we comprehend of the humidities.
And the second way is according to the places where they occur in the body, for the abscess occurring in the head is another from the abscess occurring in the buttock; and the abscess in the fleshy place is another from the abscess occurring in the joint; and to each of them is its own way of operation.
And more than abscesses are some which ought not to be perforated until the maturity of the healing in those or the completion of them.
There are other abscesses which ought to be treated when they are ripe, and not until the completion of them, such as abscesses that are near the joints, for when an abscess occurs near a joint, the being of it is prolonged until it can pour out what is in the circuit of it, and then the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted, so that it causes contraction of that limb; or it is an abscess near a principal member, and if you delay the perforation of it until its maturity, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the buttock, therefore perforate it when it is not ripe; and you ought not to perforate it cru, of no-complete digestion, but that which is near the buttock, so that you cannot touch the preon of it and it be elongated to the parts behind the buttock, and a fistula be made, or that it be done in the term of it that it not be healed. But you ought to know the hour of the perforation of the abscess, and thus it is when it is ripe.
And know that it is ripe when there is the cessation of pain and the cessation of fever, and near the diminution of the heat and of the pulse, and the acuteness of the head of the abscess, and the other signs.
And that you ought to know the perforation to be made in the place furthest from the abscess and of pus coming from the cure of the eminence.
And perforation always be by the length of the flesh or of the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the limbs or of the feet, and in the places of the tendons, of the nerves, of the arteries; and, lastly, in all places equal in which there is no reflection; for in those that are reflected, use of perforation according to that limb.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy place, then it is best that you let the perforation of it until its digestion is confirmed according to its completion, as we have said; for if you perforate it before that, it is prolonged the body of the pus of it and of much filth, and then the lips of it are hardened and the depth of it.
But some abscesses are perforated according to the latitude of the flesh or of the body as necessity demands, or according to what the limb requires.
And you ought to administer small perforation, and in large abscesses large perforation and many sections according to the diversity of the greatness of the abscesses.
And others are of abscesses in which the opening ought to be concave and be incised, when it is made so that it is like bread and made in the term that it already sticks, as that which occurs in heaps of boils and buboes.
And of those are those that are incised with section having three angles; and of those is that in which it is incised as the figure of a myrtle leaf, as the abscesses of the angles.
And of those are those in which round section and lunar section, and similar to those, are administered.
But that one to whom there is no such as his abscesses are superficial, you ought to perforate that with superficial perforation, or plane only.
And you ought when the abscess is large and has already collected much pus, that you perforate it and do not take that you extract all the pus in that hour; having extracted from it one part, and then close the abscess until the other day, and then extract a larger part, and then do that many times according to gradation until it is healed.
And especially if the patient is of frail virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old person in decrepitude, for the animal spirit many times is resolved with the egress of the pus, and then the patient dies easily, and you operate on them.
But guard this chapter with great caution, and in the perforation in which you perforate these abscesses, you ought to abstain from the plagues and consider therefore if the plague of the abscess is little, or a flat section, then you administer the qualms of it or of a counter-coction; and if the abscess is large, and the fissures of the perforation are many, then you ought to place a cloth in each tract until they meet.
And if in the abscess is incised a part of the opening or you have concaved it in the circuit, then you ought to cover it with old poultice or a thread made of cloth of it, as when you have treated bread or roots, its humidity; and strengthen that within the third day; and then process it and cure it with that which ought of the ointments until it is healed.
But if blood flow occurs during the operation, then you administer cold water and wine in which a cloth is soaked, and place it over the area of blood flow many times.
But if the blood flow persists, then you must administer a regimen and cure, and follow the powders that I have recommended in many places in this book of ours and of division.
But if it is in winter, and the place of the abscess is a place of many nerves, then you must enfund pulvils in wine and caut oil, and place those on the place.
And if it is in summer, and the places are fleshy, then you must place powders soaked in water and oil or in wine and oil, and all that be cold until it is the third day, as we have said, and then you must untie the abscess and cleanse it and administer in its cure what is convenient to it until it is healed.
And thus is what is necessary for the knowledge of the cure of abscesses universally, but according to the way of distinction I have already said of all abscesses in what manner is the way of its cure by chapters individually.
Chapter .xli.
Of the section of abscesses that come in the neck of the head.
In the neck of the head small abscesses, and so of species of nodes that contain tunics that are to their making; and the species of them are many.

And some times there are some of these abscesses that are in the head in some men with whom there is no moisture at all; the cause of which is that I incised over an abscess in the head of an old woman and brought back the abscess as it were deaf, rough, white, which could not be pierced, and if anyone were struck with that, it would plague them.

Chapter .xlii.
Of the section of scrophulas that happen in the neck.
Many times these abscesses become in the neck and in the armpits and in the groin; and some times they happen in the other parts of the body.

When the blood is separated.
