But if it is situated at the root of the thigh, then the ligament is pulled down to the bottom of the pelvis, so that the extension falls on it, and the other ligament is left below the fracture.
And similarly if the fracture is situated at the hip, then the ligament is pulled down to the hip, and the extension is made to the parts below.
And then the doctor aligns the bones with both hands while reducing it according to the natural resemblance and the bone is joined by a good connection; then, cover it with plaster and a splint, if not, the abscess will occur in the limb. But if an abscess occurs there, then leave it for a few days until the abscess has subsided, and then return to your cure.
The splint is made like this: cover the fracture with a hard bandage, and fold it two or three times, and remove any excess; and then wrap the leg until it reaches the ankle and the root of the thigh.
And introduce a long piece of felt between the thigh and the leg from the hip to the lower parts, and bring the ends of the felt from the sovereign part of both parts, and then roll over the leg and thigh what is superfluous of the bandage.
And then place on the thigh in the location of that fracture splints, and place one splint on the bone of the leg.
And then fill the vacancies between the leg and thigh with soft cloths, so that the splint is coagulated.
And then begin with a strong splint in the middle over the location of the fracture with three or four wrappings, and as much as you move away with the ligament from the location of the fracture, your splint should be smaller and lighter and softer.
And then extend both ends of the felt to the lower parts until it reaches the ankle of the foot, and tighten both ends of the splints on the other side so that the ligament is not removed from its place.
And then leave the splint on it, so that it does not cause corrosion or abscess or swelling or anything like that to the limb; and if any of those things occur, then cut it from it, and rectify what has happened again, according to what we have said many times.
But if the bone is broken in such a way that it is difficult to align, then cover it and remove it, and cure it with what precedes the recollection until it is healed.
And sometimes this fracture of the thigh is strengthened with other splints, just as we have said in the arm and the leg.
But however, in the restoration of it in this way, do not cause the patient lameness; and if it is restored alone, then apply another splint to the other leg, then it is necessary that he limp on the one that is always.
And know that the thigh is strengthened in 40 days or a few more or a few less, and all this is according to the diversity of the conditions and other dispositions.
Chapter XV.
Of the restoration of the fracture of the hip joint.
Know that a fracture of the hip joint is very difficult, but it often happens.
But if this fracture occurs, then it is not more than a fissure or crack in its parts, and this is with a plague or a few plagues, and above all, it is all affected with the feeling.
And the restoration of it is in such a way that what is broken of its parts is aligned with the fingers until it is joined and conjoined according to what is possible by equation and facility and fabrication.
And then place plaster and place a round splint on it, if it is necessary; and tighten above with a splint as is convenient.
And consider all the dispositions which we have recommended in the other fractures, as well as abscess or anything like that, so that it opposes all accidents to what is convenient until it is healed.
Chapter XVI.
Of the restoration of the fracture of the leg.
Know that in the leg there are two bones of which one is thick, and it is called by the name of the tibia; and the other is thin, and it is called fibula.
And there happen some kinds of fractures that happen to both bones of the leg, and for that reason, the restoration of it is done like the restoration of the arm, and the operation of it is one.
And if both bones are broken together, the leg is converted to all parts.
And if the thinner bone is broken, the leg is converted to the front parts.
And if the thicker bone is broken, it is thrown below, and it is one of those causes that are not to your liking.
And then administer extension, flexion, and rotation of the bones according to that alignment.
But however, if the fracture of the leg is recent and has many fragments, that the extension be less and more gently, and alleviate with your virtue.
And in the leg there is some cause for operation on the arm, and when you align the bones and that completes your entire operation, then you take pieces of wood from the palm tree which is placed below the causes which are placed in soles, and they are made of palm branches; some of those which are of small thickness, and are not of the handles, and the length of those according to the length of the leg, and from the knee to the heel.
And then envelope each piece in two envelopes according to their length, and place one on the part of the leg on one side and the other on the other side, and they be from the knee to the heel.
And then tie the two bones in three places of two extremities and in the middle place, for with this structure the leg is prohibited from bending to the right and left side, and it stays in good position.
And already is administered a splint of wood according to the length of the leg; and be placed on it the leg so that it conserve that of movement.
And most importantly, that you do this in a fracture, and when with that it is properly treated.
And then consider every day the leg and study with that by behind study, and you guard it from abscess and inflammation or other similar causes; and when it happens any cause of those, then oppose yourself to it with what is necessary before it is healed.
Chapter XVII.
Of the fracture of the talus and the bones of the foot and of the digits.
To the talus, fractures do not occur often; but to the bones of the foot, fractures occur sometimes; and to the digits of the foot, few fractures occur, and they do not occur to them but attrition in the middle of the disposition.

And then place plaster and stopa above, and place below the belly of the foot a small table to which there are two ends.

Chapter XIX.
Of the restoration of fractures of bones when it is accompanied by a plague.

Chapter .xx.
Of the cure of the node that happens in the trace of any fracture.

Chapter .xxi.

Chapter XXIII.
Of the speech in dislocation.
Dislocation is the displacement of any of the joints of the limb, so that movement is prohibited, and the figure of the limb is altered, and it brings upon the patient pains and great injuries.
Therefore, when an accident occurs to a dislocation, then it is necessary to immediately try to reduce it, and not delay that reduction, because if it is delayed, the place becomes inflamed and very difficult to reduce the dislocation.
And for this reason, one should not be bad or stretched during the time of inflammation, because often it brings spasms and intense pains.
But when this happens, then you must apply a poultice to the patient's limb, and let it rest until the inflammation subsides; and then the limb should be wrapped with warm water and oil, and then it should be reduced with facility.
And every limb should be treated with this so that the memory will come back to its place.
And you have already ordered the chapters of dislocation according to what was previously said in fractures; from the part of the body most sovereign to the part most inferior.
Chapter XXIV.
Of the cure of dislocation of the lower jaw.
So the two jaws are dislocated if not tard; and the dislocation of both is made in one of two ways: that they are pulled back to their places by little movement, and softened a little; or they are dislocated by entire dislocation and complication, so that they are softened at the junction where the saliva of the patient flows and that it cannot hold it nor be able to close its mouth, and the tongue of it be enveloped in its word.
But when the dislocation of it is slight, then in the greater dispositions it returns by itself with little cause.
But if the dislocation is entire and complicated, then it must be administered reduction of it gently, and not delayed at all.
And that the minister has the head of the patient, and meanwhile the doctor puts the tip of one of his hands in the root of the dislocation of the lower jaw from inside his mouth, if the dislocation is of one part; or that he puts both of his hands together, if the dislocation is of both parts, and the others of his hands are outside with which he pushes; and commands the patient to cease his jaws and release those to go from each part; and the doctor pushes the jaw and pushes the jaw until it returns to its place.
And if the reduction is difficult, and most of all if both jaws are dislocated together, then administer evaporation with warm water and oil, until the reduction of both is made easier and the reduction of both is not delayed at all, as we have said.
And therefore, when they return and are set, and the mouth of the patient is closed and not softened, then place on them powders of cloth with cerot, and make it of wax and oil rubbed; and then it should be lined with facility with soft linen.
And let the patient sleep on his back, and his head be standing between two pillows, so that he does not hurt either to the right or to the left; and do not let him chew for any cause; having his food be forbidden to him, until the pains are reduced and the jaws are well-set, then let him chew as he wants.
And this should be administered with facility, and do not work on the opening of the mouth of the patient, for eating and drinking and speaking, until the jaw is well-set and healed.
And if the reduction of two jaws when they are dislocated in any hour and are not converted to their places, then often this happens fever and continuous sweat, and very much is alerted the belly of the patient, and very much and vomits pure bile.
And when you see this, then you know that it is dangerous; and often dies he to whom this happens within ten days.
Chapter XXV.

Chapter .xxvi.

Chapter .xxvii.
Of the cure of dislocation of the hip.

Chapter .xxviii.
Of the cure of dislocation of the malassen, so it is of the joint that is between the arm and the hand.

And the reduction of the dislocation of that is that you place the joint of the patient's hand on a table and the minister extends the hand of that one, and the doctor places his hand or his palm on the prominence of the joint, and pushes it in while it returns to its place.
But however, it must be considered if the palm is already stayed in the belly of the hand, then the patient places the back of his hand on a table, above the extension and reduction; and if the dislocation is precedent, then the back of the hand, the position of the hand of that one intrinsically on the table, so that the hand of the doctor lies on that prominence of the joint.
And therefore, if it returns immediately, it is good; and if not, then strengthen that with a poultice, yielding the abscess and leaving it; and do not repeat this, because if not, do not endure nor can you perform the reduction of it more than days pass.
But however, the joint remains according to its tortuosity; and do not notice to the patient any cause, except that the hand is softened and cannot strengthen any cause; then you know that the nerves are cut or torn, and then it is not engendered in it except that it be strengthened with a cautery near the place of it and firmly you confer any cause.
Therefore, when the mallets is returned, then place on it the poultice which you have recomposed, and let it be left and strengthened for five days; and then it is removed and left, and the hand of it be exercised.
But if the movement of it is stayed and there occurs in it any gravity, then gently that with water cauda and with friction some times, until it is relieved.
Chapter XXIX.
Of the cure of dislocations of the said.
Sometimes the fingers are dislocated in every part.
And when a finger is dislocated of those to the back of the palm or to the belly of it, then stretch the finger and push the dislocation of it with your thumbs, until it returns.
And then support the head of the finger, and suspend that which is dislocated, and leave it for two days.
And then suspend that and extend that until straight it be healed in that its day.
And when it will be night, tie that according to that narration, and do not cease to untie that in the day and exercise with movement, and tie that at night; and do this for some days until it be straight.
And do similar with this, if it is dislocated to the belly of the hand, and tie that to that part and do with this your first operation, until it be healed.
And similarly do with this when it is dislocated to the other parts.
Chapter XXX.
Of the cure of dislocations of the vertebrae of the back.
When there occurs to any of the vertebrae of the back or of the neck a dislocation complicated, and the moved vertebrae are removed from their places, then in that there is no cure, because death seizes the patient.
And a sign of this is that the digestion of the patient is outside its will, and it cannot retain that; and many times are softened some members of it or two legs of it or two arms of it, or one of those; or a vertebra is removed from its place, because many times it is removed and many times is made the removal of those to four parts.
Therefore, that is already removed to the parts behind and is named gelbozit.
But the cure of it is that then consider if the gelbozit occurs from puerility, because then in that there is no cure nor of that there is healing of all.
But in that which comes from a blow or from percussion or similar to those, already said the Ancients the ways of cure with sermons prolixs, of which the most returns with prophecy; but I have already and abbreviated of that of which the little excuse of the trop of it, for the my better proximity to the better understanding exposition, with the which I have this exposed and formatted ex instrument divers of that with the which I will show this and expose that.
And of those there is no cured except that which occurs in the back properly with that which I have recomposed.
And it is that the patient be extended on his face upon a bed  near a wall, and be extended behind him a soft instrument so that the feet of him be not lifted.
And then a straight stick be placed, fixed in the ground at the extremity of the bed near the head of him, and another stick in the opposite extremity of the bed under the feet of him.
And the minister holds the stick, and it not be fastened in a ditch; and another minister holds the other according to that form.
And then envelope over the head of the patient and behind the little limbs lion firm; and extend the extremity of the limb to the stick which is above the head of him, and tie that in it; and then strengthen the other ligament over the hips of him the denols of him, and below the legs of him; and then adjust all the ligaments and tie those in the other stick which is above the feet of him.
And then the minister, having casqued, extends the ligament to the part of the shaft, and do not be removed the two shafts and ligaments from their places in which they are placed, but however do not be stopped as we have said.
And the doctor places his palms on the spine with strength while it returns, or that which places on that a table, and then that adjust on the table his feet while it returns.
But if it does not return in this way, then take a table of which the latitude or longitude is in average of three brasss, and carve in the wall of which we have said that is near the patient a place in which enter the extremity of the table. And then place the majority of the table on the spine, and the doctor places his feet on the other extremity, and tightens well while the spine is shortened and that it returns to its place.
And if you wish, open with a turn the which is revolved with the hand; and is that you place on the ground the head of the patient in the rear of the pug two shafts, the longitude of which is of an arm, and place the head of him in the rear of the pug also two shafts; and be the longitude that is between each shaft a palm, and already is made in each shaft a groove in which runs the turn, and each one be stopped on the ground so that it is not moved.
And be also a shaft round in which is the turn, and be revolved in the two grooves of the two shafts.
And in the extremity of it is a groove in which is formed the shaft, the length of which is a palm with that which is revolved; and in the two other shafts is similar to that.
And then tighten the ligaments that you have straightened in the feet of the patient in the groove which is of the head of him, and the ligaments that you have straightened in the thighs of him in the turn which is of the feet of him.
And then place each turn and stay a minister that twists the turn with his hand, and the doctor aligns the spine according to what we have said.
And as soon as the spine is returned and the place is aligned, then cover that you place a poultice of dried album of egg, and then cotton; and then place on the poultice a board of which the latitude is of three digits or around those, and the length of it is the quantity that engulfs the place of the hollow, and on the part of the spine as well.
And then tie with the ligaments which we have said, and use the patient of subtle nourishment while it is healing.
And if there remains any prominence in the place at the end of the healing, then cover that medicines be administered which soften and lubricate with administration of the table for a long time, which we have recommended; and already is administered in that place a sheet of lead.
And some times an accident happens prominence in the rear of the spines of the two, and it is cured by that dislocation; and it is that bone which already protrudes because it is not to be done proscription to it with this medicine, for very strong it will make you to happen death.
Chapter .xxxi.
Of the cure of a dislocated hip.
Know that the joint of the hip and the joint of the muscle should not be dislocated only, and accidents do not happen to those that happen to the other joints of small movement and concavity.
And the joint of the hip is dislocated in four ways, because it is dislocated to the front parts, or to the back parts, or to the front parts, or to the back parts.
And mostly it is dislocated to the front parts, and few to the front parts or to the back parts.
And the sign of the dislocation of it to the front parts is that, when you adjust the leg of the healthy patient with the patient, it is longer and the thigh is more prominent than of the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend his foot with the leg, and it is the place that if the leg is dislocated, it is postemated of cautery, so that the head of the thigh has already arrived here.
And the sign of that one which happens dislocation is to the back parts, is that the accidents of it are contraries to this accident.
And the sign of that one which happens dislocation to the front parts is that it expands its thigh according to completion, but however it does not bend that part of pain that is in the thigh, and if it persists to go and cannot above that to the front parts; and the urine of it is retained and the groin of it is postemated, and it walks on the crutch.
And the sign of that one which happens dislocation to the back parts is that it does not expand the thigh, nor can it bend that part that bends the groin, and the thigh of it is shorter than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is of that place.
But the reduction of the species of this dislocation is that you consider, then, if the dislocation is old and antique, that it is already attached with that, then you administer reduction of it and remains according to its disposition, then it is not in that cure of all; and therefore it is not to be done proscription in that.
But in the case of which the dislocation is recent, and is one of the four species of dislocation, then take hold of it so that you turn the joint and extend it to the inner and outer parts, and move it to the right and left, for it will return quickly and does not need other care.
But if it does not return in this manner, then have you prepare a strong minister and extend the leg of him from the rear part, or by his hands, or by a bandage which is tied above the knee; and another minister extend the hand of him from below so that he puts his hands behind the heels of him; and then tighten with a bandage on the root of the groin, and hold another minister the extremity of the bandage.
And the extension of him or from the inner part to the angle of the shoulder, or from the rear part to the part of the back.
And the extension of all those at once while the patient be elevated with his body from the ground and remains hanging.
And this kind of extension is common to all four.
And therefore if the dislocation returns with what we have said, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary for all species that we say of the proper cure.
In the reduction of the proper, when it is dislocated, and the dislocation is in the inner parts, then have the patient be laid down on his side; and then place the ligaments on the root of the groin in that place which is between the head of the groin and the place which is below the shoulder; and then extend the ligament above the part of the shoulder to the highest part of the collarbone.
And then another minister firmly grasps the arms of him, and embrace the thick part of the groin of the patient and extend to the outer parts by vehement extension, for that returns to its place.
And this kind is of the lightest cure with which this member is reduced than the others.
But if it is excused upon you and do not obey the entrance with this kind of cure of all, then have the two legs of the patient be tied together with a strong, light bandage, on both the ankles and both the knees.
And the length of each one of them by the quantity of four fingers, and the leg of the patient extended more than the other by the quantity of two fingers.
And then the patient be suspended over the head of the pole, and that be in the middle; and the length of him from the ground the quantity of two arms.
And then command a strong young man to press the head of the groin, and be suspended with the patient another young man, and the other young man presses the groin with strength impelling, for the joint returns to its place with speed.
But in the proper reduction, when the dislocation is in the outer part, then have the patient lie on his stomach according to what we have recounted in the having flatulence; and be tightened the ligament over the leg of the patient properly and over the feet of him.
And then two poles be placed, one at the feet of him, and the other at the head; and then be placed poles adjusted in the middle of the groin laid upon which damp cloths be enveloped, so that the patient be not harmed because the pole be between the thighs of him, for that the extension to the rear parts not be pulled.
And then each minister extends his part, and the physician with his hand engulfs the reduction according to the art.
And when the dislocation is in the front parts, then have the leg be extended slightly, and it is according to this same narration about groin; and the physician places the palm of his right hand over the groin of the patient, and then shortens that with the other hand, and with that shortening pauses that extended to the rear parts to the part of the knee.
And if the dislocation is in the rear parts, then have the patient not be extended to the rear parts, and be elevated above the ground; have it be placed upon a hard cause, as it is commanded if the dislocation is in the outer parts, according to what we have said of the placing of him upon two widths; and it is upon his face and the ligaments be extended, according to what we have said, there is no harm.
And have compression be administered with a table upon the place where the joint is.
Therefore, as the reduction is complicated according to what is commanded — and the sign of the reduction of him is not hidden from you, and it is that you extend the two legs of the patient, and when you see those engulfs and the patient extends his leg and expands that his excuse, then you know that the member according to what is commanded is returned — and then you adjust two thighs and pause poultice and extend with bandage so that the width is not harmed in any of the parts; and adhere the patient to rest for three days or for four.
And then untie the bandage and the poultice, and compare one leg with the other.
Now, if you see those bumps in the clothing, then you know the dislocation is already fixed, and therefore let the patient go.
And if you see any cause of softening, then you return and plaster it, and stretch it according to your first structure, and leave it for three days.
And then unwrap it, and make him delay in walking for some days, until it is comforted.
Chapter .xxxii.
Of the cure of dislocation of the knee.
The knee is dislocated in three ways, for it is dislocated to the outside parts, and to the inside parts, and to the parts behind, to the parts in front; and to the front parts it is not dislocated.
And the sign of dislocation of it is that you command the patient to apply his leg to the thigh; then you know that the knee is dislocated.
And the restoration of all the ways of it is that you make the patient straight, so that he already extends his leg, if he can over that; adhere your two to the face of it, and place his foot between your feet; and then make adhere the knee of it to your palms, and hold those between your fingers on the knee of it with strength, and another minister extends his leg while the knee returns to its place.
And the sign of the return of it is that his leg adheres to the thigh with lightness without labor.
And then plaster it and make the leg adhere to the thigh, and then tie those immediately with a bandage for three days or for four, and then unwrap them.
And do not use the patient for walking for some days, until it is healed and comforted.
But if the reduction of it to you is excused, then administer strong extension with ligaments of which in the cure of the hernia preceding narration.
Chapter .xxxiii.
Of the cure of the dislocation of the ankle.
The ankle some times is dislocated by small movement, and some times it is dislocated according to compliment, and the dislocation of it is made either to the inside parts or to the outside parts.
And the sign of the dislocation of it is that you see the ankle inflated proceeding to the part to which it is dislocated.
But the cure of the dislocation of it is of lightness reduction, and it is that it be extended with ease with the hands and be bandaged while it returns.
But in the cure of it when it is dislocated according to compliment, cover that you make the patient straight, and hold that one minister strong and valiant of the back part of it in the middle place of it.
And then you with your right hand the foot of the most sovereign part, and with your left hand of the part most behind of the foot in the place of the ankle.
And then you pull the foot to you with your right hand, and with the left for two times, and then extend with the left; and you push the foot of the foot with the right, so that the leg works.
And do this two times according to that we have counted.
And then push the foot of the foot to the leg the third time, and you are at the ankle.
Therefore if it returns in one time or in two according to this manner, and if you see the foot bandaged, it is good; and if not, then over it iterate the operation, for that it returns.
But if to you is forbidden the reduction of it with that which we have recounted, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and stretch a small piece of cloth on the ground firmly, and that it lie between the thighs of it, and you have already enveloped over it cloth so that it does not harm the patient.
And then the minister of it holds its thighs, and another minister extends the leg with its hands or with ligaments that lie on the collar of the foot; and then extend that each minister against extension of its part, and the cloth be extended between the thighs of the patient, holding it, so that the body of it is not pulled to the behind parts, according to its extension.
And then the physician bandages the dislocation with its hands, and another minister holds the healthy thigh to the behind parts, for the dislocation returns with ease.
And therefore when the dislocation returns and is declared to you the health of the reduction of it, then pause plaster and stretch that with ligaments strongly, and tie the foot with ligaments to the leg.
And cover that you fear or guard yourself of the nerves which are behind on the ankle, so that the ligament over it not be vehement and harm it strongly.
And then leave it for two days or three; and if the ligament is softened, stretch it.
And then unwrap it on the third day or on the fourth, and prohibit the patient from movement for 40 days. But if it is forced to go before that space, it is not made secure that the dislocation is not dissolved and corrupted over it, and then that it does not receive cure.
And if it happens to it a boil, then cover that you administer in the reduction of it that which I preceded our narration, in another place of cure and of embrocation, until it is healed.
Chapter XXXIV.
Of the cure of dislocation of the toes.
So that the one that is dislocated be straightened with little extension of his work; and that which is not difficult, raise it lightly.
But if the dislocation is in some joints of the foot, then make the patient place his foot on a level surface of the ground or on a table, and be standing thus as if he were going.
And then stand beside the patient, and place your foot on that which is above the joints, and press it with your foot with force until it returns, and that you see it straightened and does not appear in the area prominence.
And then place under the foot of the patient a table that supports the whole foot, which has two ends, and strengthen it with a decent and firm structure for three days; and then untie it and make the patient rest from walking for many days, until it is straightened and its return is assured.
Chapter XXXV.
Of the kinds of dislocations that are made with plague or with fracture or with any of them together.
When any of those causes happen, and you are engaged in the cure of it and in its restoration, many times death occurs.
And for this reason, you should not presume on the cure of it, but rather he who is wise in the art, of long usage, merciful and compassionate, tardy, not bold nor presumptuous; and who uses in the beginning of medicines that cause abscesses, only so much, and leaves the patient to the divine judgment, but to him whom you hope for salvation from perdition, with the alleviation of the disease, and in which you see some hope. And therefore, strive as soon as possible to make the reduction of it at the beginning of the cause, before an abscess forms.
And therefore, if the member returns as we want, then administer the regimen which causes an abscess and cures the plague with what is convenient to it of the dried herbs.
And if the dislocation is with a fracture and happens in the bones that are separated, then you pierce the ligament of them, and do in that what we have said in the simple ailments of this which is preceded in the places of those.
And guard and avoid according to your virtue that of the instrument in the ways of fear according to what has preceded me in your teaching; for this is better to you, you should owe your Creator, and more permanent to your glory, and more greetings to your true body in your time. Thus ends the words of Albucasim perfectly, of which may God be the benefit. Amen.
